  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_50170949-2b39-40a4-8fb4-6121570e52da'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6671858228218745863"><b>In a highly awaited new novel, Kate DiCamillo conjures a haunting fable about trusting the unexpected — and making the extraordinary come true.</b><br/><br/>What if? Why not? Could it be?<br/><br/>When a fortuneteller's tent appears in the market square of the city of Baltese, orphan Peter Augustus Duchene knows the questions that he needs to ask: Does his sister still live? And if so, how can he</span>
  <span id="freeText6671858228218745863" style="display:none"><b>In a highly awaited new novel, Kate DiCamillo conjures a haunting fable about trusting the unexpected — and making the extraordinary come true.</b><br /><br />What if? Why not? Could it be?<br /><br />When a fortuneteller's tent appears in the market square of the city of Baltese, orphan Peter Augustus Duchene knows the questions that he needs to ask: Does his sister still live? And if so, how can he find her? The fortuneteller's mysterious answer (an elephant! An elephant will lead him there!) sets off a chain of events so remarkable, so impossible, that you will hardly dare to believe it’s true. With atmospheric illustrations by fine artist Yoko Tanaka, here is a dreamlike and captivating tale that could only be narrated by Newbery Medalist Kate DiCamillo. In this timeless fable, she evokes the largest of themes — hope and belonging, desire and compassion — with the lightness of a magician’s touch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6671858228218745863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2728235185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8009092290263872753"><i>The Magician's Elephant</i> by Kate DiCamillo is a mysterious and magical story about a boy named Peter who has been orphaned, and the unlikely appearance of an elephant who helps him find his way. <br/><br/>The story takes place in the city of Baltese, which is filled with people of different classes. It's a cold and very dark winter with minimal sunshine. Peter currently lives with his guardian--a soldier named Vilna who fought in war alongside Peter's father. Sadly, Peter's mother died just after the birth</span>
  <span id="freeText8009092290263872753" style="display:none"><i>The Magician's Elephant</i> by Kate DiCamillo is a mysterious and magical story about a boy named Peter who has been orphaned, and the unlikely appearance of an elephant who helps him find his way. <br /><br />The story takes place in the city of Baltese, which is filled with people of different classes. It's a cold and very dark winter with minimal sunshine. Peter currently lives with his guardian--a soldier named Vilna who fought in war alongside Peter's father. Sadly, Peter's mother died just after the birth of his baby sister. Even though Peter has been told that his sister also died at birth, he has a subtle remembrance of her crying and feels that she may still be alive. One day, after being sent to the marketplace to purchase food, Peter discovers a fortuneteller. He asks the fortuneteller of his sister, and indeed, he's told that she lives. <br /><br /><i>"You must follow the elephant," said the fortune teller. "She will lead you there."</i><br /><br />Peter is shocked, excited, and also confused. Could this really be true? Why has he been lied to all these years? Peter knows he must find the elephant and attempt to locate his sister, but he can't do it alone.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the way the characters were written in this story; there's enough left open to let the reader imagine. When I first started reading this with my kids, we were all reading intently, but without a whole lot of amusement my kids became disinterested. We still wanted to find out what would happen with Peter and the other characters, but the story fell a little flat for us. Don't get me wrong, the book is written well and it's beautiful at times with themes of love, forgiveness, and most of all: hope. <br /><br /><i>"Looking out over the city, Peter decided that it was a terrible and complicated thing to hope, and that it might be easier, instead, to despair."</i><br /><br />I did love the ending (although predictable) with how each of the characters were impacted by the elephant and essentially changed. It had a nice conclusion. We also loved the illustrations. This was an enjoyable read that I'll still recommend. <br /><br />3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="8009092290263872753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7575922339020484318" style="display:none">This book was like eating crème brûlée, with the satisfaction of breaking the burnt sugar spine to eat the warm and sweet center. It would be perfect to have it read aloud while you fall asleep to falling snow. <br /><br />Favorite Quote: <br /><br />Magic is always impossible...It begins with the impossible and ends with the impossible and is impossible in between. That is why it is magic. <br /><br />It is a bad thing to have love and nowhere to put it. <br /><br />He had been so lonely, so desperately, hopelessly lonely for so long. He might very well spend the rest of his life in prison, alone. And he understood that what he wanted now was something much simpler, much more complicated than the magic he had performed. What he wanted was to turn to somebody and take hold of their hand and look up with them and marvel at the snow falling from the sky. “This,” he wanted to say to someone he loved and who loved him in return. “This.”<br /><br />The undoing is almost always more difficult than the doing. </span>

<div id="review_2028662498" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2028662498" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2028662498?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2028662498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9906338694073068035">Kate DiCamillo has a unique voice. This is my 6th book from her and I don’t think I can compare her to any other author. The way she thinks… it’s different and unexpected, but in a good way. <br/><br/>This is the story of a little boy who tries to find his sister with the help of other characters, including a peculiar, magical elephant. Except, while Peter is technically the main character, since the story revolves around him, the author focuses on many other people.<br/><br/>And even though that makes things inter</span>
  <span id="freeText9906338694073068035" style="display:none">Kate DiCamillo has a unique voice. This is my 6th book from her and I don’t think I can compare her to any other author. The way she thinks… it’s different and unexpected, but in a good way. <br /><br />This is the story of a little boy who tries to find his sister with the help of other characters, including a peculiar, magical elephant. Except, while Peter is technically the main character, since the story revolves around him, the author focuses on many other people.<br /><br />And even though that makes things interesting and moving fast – there was always someone to talk about, something to focus on – I found it problematic in the sense that it makes it hard to connect to the characters. It was like the author absolutely wanted us to learn everyone’s back-stories to not forget them, in a forceful way. <br /><br />The writing is excellent. This is a children’s book, so obviously it’s young, but very enjoyable for a mature audience too. Miss DiCamillo has a way with words. No wonder she’s ‘‘America’s Beloved Storyteller’’. Quite a prestigious title. <br /><br />I can picture myself reading this out loud to a kid. Could make for a wonderful—magical—bedtime story. Not realistic in the slightest but the emotions and themes are true. Strong ties to family are beautiful. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9906338694073068035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer67613549" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer938626899892168913">This is my first Kate DiCamillo book and it has made a deep impression on me. The best "children's books" work on an adult level as well. This one is the best I have read in a long while. She writes beautifully, and her characters have more depth than you would expect. The plot falls into place as a small boy squanders his guardian's money on getting his fortune read. When he hears that a elephant will take him to his sister (who he has been told died at birth) he struggles with what is true and</span>
  <span id="freeText938626899892168913" style="display:none">This is my first Kate DiCamillo book and it has made a deep impression on me. The best "children's books" work on an adult level as well. This one is the best I have read in a long while. She writes beautifully, and her characters have more depth than you would expect. The plot falls into place as a small boy squanders his guardian's money on getting his fortune read. When he hears that a elephant will take him to his sister (who he has been told died at birth) he struggles with what is true and what to believe. You with find the characters in the city of Baltese magical and not just the magician, but the stonecutter, the beggar, Sister Marie of the orphange and more. The story is over in 200 pages and that is much too soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="938626899892168913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78322600" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/378822-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189873342p2/378822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78322600?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/378822-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/378822-wendy?shelf=2009-award-possibilities">2009-award-possibilities</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78322600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6520426818946279089">Part of me wants to say I loved this book, that it verges on Trumpet of the Swan or Jane Langton territory, and part of me is afraid I've been sucked into the next Jonathan Livingston Seagull or Kahlil Gibran. (I finally put my finger on what this book reminds me of: The Polar Express. And that's perfect, because I can never decide about that book, either.)<br/><br/>I think the prose is very lovely, and I don't always go for lovely prose, but this is funny, too. There's humor and pathos both in the contin</span>
  <span id="freeText6520426818946279089" style="display:none">Part of me wants to say I loved this book, that it verges on Trumpet of the Swan or Jane Langton territory, and part of me is afraid I've been sucked into the next Jonathan Livingston Seagull or Kahlil Gibran. (I finally put my finger on what this book reminds me of: The Polar Express. And that's perfect, because I can never decide about that book, either.)<br /><br />I think the prose is very lovely, and I don't always go for lovely prose, but this is funny, too. There's humor and pathos both in the continually repeated lines, like "I intended only lilies".<br /><br />I have no idea whether I would have liked this as a kid. I have no idea whether kids will like it now. But I like it now. It evokes art to me (that isn't as pretentious as it sounds, or at least I hope it isn't, but I was an art history major and it's how I think): Impressionist in style and setting and mood, and then Italian Renaissance for complicated reasons that have to do with Florence keeping a pet giraffe. And I like anything that makes me think about art.<br /><br />Newbery? No, people would flip. And I don't think you could really call the development of plot distinguished.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6520426818946279089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83101405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83101405" />
    <a title="Linden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1509047-linden"><img alt="Linden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220907811p2/1509047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83101405?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linden" href="/user/show/1509047-linden">Linden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer83101405&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83101405" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253173982803863592"> I've been a steady fan of DiCamillo's past work but was disappointed with <u>The Magician's Elephant</u>. The story is about a boy, Peter Augustus Duchene, who, on the way to buy fish and bread, spends his guardian's coin on a visit to a fortuneteller. He hears that his sister is not dead as he had believed and that an elephant will help him find her. That evening, at a show in the town opera house, a magician's error causes an elephant to drop from the sky through its roof and inadvertently cripple a</span>
  <span id="freeText8253173982803863592" style="display:none"> I've been a steady fan of DiCamillo's past work but was disappointed with <u>The Magician's Elephant</u>. The story is about a boy, Peter Augustus Duchene, who, on the way to buy fish and bread, spends his guardian's coin on a visit to a fortuneteller. He hears that his sister is not dead as he had believed and that an elephant will help him find her. That evening, at a show in the town opera house, a magician's error causes an elephant to drop from the sky through its roof and inadvertently cripple a woman.<br /><br />The structure of the story is that of disparate threads that gradually converge and then interweave: the magician, a beggar, a sculptor, the boy, his sister, a nun, and the woman. One of the starred reviews, this from the School Library Journal, for example, declares that "DiCamillo's carefully crafted prose creates an evocative aura of timelessness for a story that is, in fact, timeless." This I've found to be true of her other work, blending elements like a good cook with delicious language and pace.<br /><br />There were certainly parts I enjoyed in this book. I quite liked DiCamillo's rendering of the society woman who pre-empted ownership of the elephant after its unusual arrival in order to maintain ascendancy in her social circle. She widened the doorway of her house to admit the elephant then allowed people to view it, captive in her house and the viewers in her thrall. This part rang true to me of human nature. However I admit I had been preoccupied all along, fretting about the elephant. Had it been injured in its fall through sky, roof and thence onto the woman who occupied the seat upon which it fell? I envisioned the splintering of beams, broken plaster and worse. Yet no mention of an injury save that of the woman it landed upon. For me, there was something about the lack of information about the elephant except for its terrible unhappiness in the woman's house that made it seem an authorial device, becoming three dimensional only when it served the tale.<br /><br />In this story, though quite short compared to her other work, I fidgeted (rare for me), trying to urge the story forward. It reminded me of that uncomfortable dream in which a desperate need to run is countered by being able to move with great effort only in slow motion. All in all, it seemed a very thin broth for the number of pages I had to consume. <br /><br />I look forward to more of her work of the caliber of <u>The Tale of Despereaux</u> and <u>The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane</u>, both of which rightly earned their places on our library shelf. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8253173982803863592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2514197792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2514197792" />
    <a title="Henry Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14734360-henry-martin"><img alt="Henry Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442649786p2/14734360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2514197792?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Martin" href="/user/show/14734360-henry-martin">Henry Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14734360-henry-martin?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14734360-henry-martin?shelf=permanent-collection">permanent-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2514197792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9755848286612115654">In a typical DiCamillo style, The Magician's Elephant is a complex story disguised as a children's tale, although, compared to Edward Tulane or Tiger Rising, this one is more subtle in its message. <br/><br/>Take a sleepy city (which could be anywhere) with its upper, middle, and poor classes, and make the story come alive. In this case, it all begins with a little orphan boy being raised by a feverish soldier who fought alongside the boy's father. The little boy is being raised to be a soldier, to live o</span>
  <span id="freeText9755848286612115654" style="display:none">In a typical DiCamillo style, The Magician's Elephant is a complex story disguised as a children's tale, although, compared to Edward Tulane or Tiger Rising, this one is more subtle in its message. <br /><br />Take a sleepy city (which could be anywhere) with its upper, middle, and poor classes, and make the story come alive. In this case, it all begins with a little orphan boy being raised by a feverish soldier who fought alongside the boy's father. The little boy is being raised to be a soldier, to live on moldy bread and impossible small fishes. The boy's life, it seems, lacks light. <br /><br />Throw in mysterious fortune teller, with an even more mysterious message, and things begin to change. How? For one, the boy now has hope. Oh, the powerful force that breathes life into dull things. Hope, in a way, is impossible. Equally impossible to bear, and impossible to extinguish. Hope, the main driving force behind DiCamillo's characters I love in every one of her books, is what makes the difference between the status quo and the unexpected. <br /><br />In the same city, there lives a policeman and his wife, childless, set in their ways. But the policeman also hopes, asking the important, "What if . . ."<br /><br />And there lives a noblewoman, a powerful woman who wants to be entertained during a magic show. The aging magician, one who has been the laughing stock of the town, is about to perform the last act of his life, when he asks the impossible, "What if . . ."<br /><br />And in an orphanage, not far away, a little girl dreams of the impossible, and her dream revisits her over and over, until she asks; while a crazy stone-cutter dreams of making one more statue, a beggar sings of the things to come (if only anyone would listen), and another noble woman pulls the strings to become the center of the social season setting the impossible into motion. <br /><br />In the Magician's Elephant, DiCamillo paints a vivid portrait of lost hopes, crushed dreams, impossible desires, and the consequences of losing one's self. She explores very human drives and desires, social classes, and the unfortunate status quo. But she also shows that nothing is set in stone, and that hope, no matter how ridiculous, makes people do great and selfless things. <br /><br />Another great book by a very talented author. Highly recommended to read along with young readers (great topics for a discussion) or to read by yourself when you tire of all things adult, and want to escape into a world of wonder. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9755848286612115654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_71142835" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71142835" />
    <a title="Renee Wallace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2439472-renee-wallace"><img alt="Renee Wallace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449948812p2/2439472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71142835?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renee Wallace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renee Wallace" href="/user/show/2439472-renee-wallace">Renee Wallace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71142835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8083812379392381203">Wow, Reader, if you make up your mind about what to read/purchase/borrow at your library from these reviews, then pay attention to this one! :-) <br/><br/>I keep wondering, with each new book, Can Kate DiCamillo really do it again? Can she possibly make the magic again? And the answer is always a resounding YES. <br/><br/>I do not recall the last time I actually wept while reading a book, but I not only did while reading this one, I even know the page number that brought it about--but you have to weep on your own t</span>
  <span id="freeText8083812379392381203" style="display:none">Wow, Reader, if you make up your mind about what to read/purchase/borrow at your library from these reviews, then pay attention to this one! :-) <br /><br />I keep wondering, with each new book, Can Kate DiCamillo really do it again? Can she possibly make the magic again? And the answer is always a resounding YES. <br /><br />I do not recall the last time I actually wept while reading a book, but I not only did while reading this one, I even know the page number that brought it about--but you have to weep on your own timetable, not someone else's! :-) <br /><br />What amazes me is how the author actually includes, among all the magic, all the wonder, the dreams, the hopes, the heartaches, she actually works in there the practical means for dealing with those "dark nights of the soul," which, dreadfully, each young reader will probably face some day. When the hero is at his lowest ebb, she has him look his terrible loss head-on, dead-on; and he faces it, and grows stronger. Also, nearing that dreadful point, he is urged to eat. Such a simple lesson, and yet each child needs to know: if you can get your basic needs met, you can face what must be faced. When in despair, you must take care of the body, in order to take care of the soul. <br /><br />Best of all, she asks the reader these questions, with this story: Can dreams come true? Can the impossible ever really happen? Can happy endings not only happen, but happen with such deep meaning? <br /><br />And she manages all of that without soppiness, syrup, goo, or becoming maudlin. <br /><br />She must believe, as I believe, as children long to believe, that good happens. Prayers are answered. Hope does indeed beat eternal, and for good reason. <br /><br />I LOVE it. I absolutely love it. Ms. DiCamillo, I salute you. <br /><br />And P.S. I love Iddo. <br /><br />Oh, wait! Ms. Tanaka! Your illustrations help make the magic, too. The elephant's eyes! Incredible. All your illustrations, actually, are incredible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8083812379392381203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_78925590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78925590" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/271355-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363406354p2/271355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78925590?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/271355-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/271355-jess?shelf=juv">juv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/271355-jess?shelf=mock-newbery-2010">mock-newbery-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/271355-jess?shelf=orca-2011-2012">orca-2011-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78925590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer602038184257364773">Oh boy, I wanted to like this one. I adored <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37190.The_Tale_of_Despereaux_Being_the_Story_of_a_Mouse__a_Princess__Some_Soup_and_a_Spool_of_Thread' title='The Tale of Despereaux Being the Story of a Mouse, a Princess, Some Soup and a Spool of Thread by Kate DiCamillo' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Tale of Despereaux Being the Story of a Mouse, a Princess, Some Soup and a Spool of Thread</a>, I enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/357664.Because_of_Winn_Dixie' title='Because of Winn-Dixie by Kate DiCamillo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Because of Winn-Dixie</a>, I was fascinated with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37186.The_Miraculous_Journey_of_Edward_Tulane' title='The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane by Kate DiCamillo' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane</a> (and loved the illustrations), but this left me a little cold. I've been trying to put my finger on it, since this is on this year's OLA Mock Newbery list and I'll have to back up my opinion. I didn't feel that it went deep enough - it stayed on the surface of a po</span>
  <span id="freeText602038184257364773" style="display:none">Oh boy, I wanted to like this one. I adored <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37190.The_Tale_of_Despereaux_Being_the_Story_of_a_Mouse__a_Princess__Some_Soup_and_a_Spool_of_Thread" title="The Tale of Despereaux Being the Story of a Mouse, a Princess, Some Soup and a Spool of Thread by Kate DiCamillo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tale of Despereaux Being the Story of a Mouse, a Princess, Some Soup and a Spool of Thread</a>, I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/357664.Because_of_Winn_Dixie" title="Because of Winn-Dixie by Kate DiCamillo" rel="nofollow noopener">Because of Winn-Dixie</a>, I was fascinated with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37186.The_Miraculous_Journey_of_Edward_Tulane" title="The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane by Kate DiCamillo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane</a> (and loved the illustrations), but this left me a little cold. I've been trying to put my finger on it, since this is on this year's OLA Mock Newbery list and I'll have to back up my opinion. I didn't feel that it went deep enough - it stayed on the surface of a potentially interesting story, and that simplicity, which felt intentional, ended up feeling too much like a fable for me. I detest novel-length fables. I want characters, not archetypes. I just skimmed across the surface and thought, "pretty sentence" and waited to be caught up in the story. There were too many characters introduced too quickly and too briefly. This is, perhaps, a matter of taste. I'll have to work on argument before the discussion rolls around in January. </span>
  <a data-text-id="602038184257364773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_194093218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194093218" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194093218?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8150045-the-magician-s-elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194093218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5036900428795976291"><b> 4.5 stars </b><br/>Sometimes I miss the sense of childlike wonder that kids have. Last night one of my little cousins was making up a tall-tell about his mother making him pay rent. The fiction just flew from his lips naturally. It's like the realm of make-believe lives right below the surface and kids can jump in anytime without any effort.<br/><br/>Maybe that's why I keep falling for sweet innocent books that remind me of fairytales. Maybe I'm trying to recapture something I've lost along the path to adulthood.</span>
  <span id="freeText5036900428795976291" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars </b><br />Sometimes I miss the sense of childlike wonder that kids have. Last night one of my little cousins was making up a tall-tell about his mother making him pay rent. The fiction just flew from his lips naturally. It's like the realm of make-believe lives right below the surface and kids can jump in anytime without any effort.<br /><br />Maybe that's why I keep falling for sweet innocent books that remind me of fairytales. Maybe I'm trying to recapture something I've lost along the path to adulthood. Whatever the reason I love books like Goose Girl, Princess Academy and the latest, The Magician's Elephant.<br /><br />It's such a sweet beautiful little book. The book contains a magic that my normal YA can never capture. It's the magic of being a 10-year-old child where the world is so big and anything is possible.<br /><br />The Magician's Elephant completely charmed me. The language is whimsical and witty. It manages to be poetic and unobtrusive. It's simply perfect and I can't imagine the book being written any other way. As I read, I kept hearing a gentle lyrical voice (think of the Pushing Daisies narration) reading the story to me. Almost every page had a clever or poetic phrase. Never have I been so grateful for my Kindle highlighting feature and I'm not typically an underliner.<br /><br /><i>"Looking out over the city, Peter decided that it was a terrible and complicated thing to hope, and that it might be easier, instead to despair." </i><br /><br />The book has an usual premise, a little boy named Peter spends his bread money at a fortuneteller because he wants the truth. The truth he gets is wonderful, yet impossible His sister, who his guardian said was stillborn, lives. She lives! We get the sense of joy and responsibility that Peter feels towards his sister immediately. First he needs to find her. The fortuneteller says the elephant will show him the way. But there are no elephants anywhere near where Peter lives so the wonderful beautiful hope he is given seems cruelly impossible.<br /><br />Lucky for Peter, this is a book that believes in the impossible.<br /><br />The Magician's Elephant is a hopeful story. I think all ages will appreciate the beautiful poetic language and deceptively simple story. The story manages to capture the wonder of a child and a child's audacity to believe in the impossible.<br /><br /><i>"What are we to make of a world where stars shine bright in the midst of so much darkness and gloom?"</i><br /><br />It's hard to do this book justice. The Magician's Elephant is a bright, shining, audaciously hopeful book. It's a joy to read And I know it'll be a regular re-read. I loved the feeling of reading this book and I know I'll want to experience that again. The book is magic. For a brief few pages it gave me back my childhood, my sense of wonder and reminded the word is a very big, impressive and magical place. And that maybe, just maybe, believing in the impossible is the best way to live.<br /><br /><b>Currently only $1.99 for Kindle. Don't know how long that deal will last. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5036900428795976291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73782125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73782125" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1390765-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296562176p2/1390765.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73782125?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/1390765-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73782125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11710932460929435967">The Magician's Elephant is a wonderful whimsical story which includes some fabulous black and white illustrations, by Yoko Tanaka. The illustrations add to the beauty of this story which takes place some 200 years ago.<br/><br/>Peter Augustus Duchene is a ten year old orphan. When his guardian sends him out with one coin to purchase some food in the Baltese market square, he sees a fortune teller's tent, and has something more pressing than food on his mind. Peter was told that his sister was dead, and th</span>
  <span id="freeText11710932460929435967" style="display:none">The Magician's Elephant is a wonderful whimsical story which includes some fabulous black and white illustrations, by Yoko Tanaka. The illustrations add to the beauty of this story which takes place some 200 years ago.<br /><br />Peter Augustus Duchene is a ten year old orphan. When his guardian sends him out with one coin to purchase some food in the Baltese market square, he sees a fortune teller's tent, and has something more pressing than food on his mind. Peter was told that his sister was dead, and the question he must ask the fortune teller is----does his sister live, and if so, how can he find her? The fortune teller answers the question by saying "follow the elephant", and tells him that the elephant will lead him there.<br /><br />When a magician's act goes terribly wrong, and an elephant falls from the ceiling of the opera house, an unbelievable chain of events are set into motion.<br /><br />The Magician's Elephant is written for middle school aged children. It is a dark, but hopeful tale with a wonderful cast of charming characters. It is a wonderful story that shows us what can happen to those who believe. I am confident this delightful story will reawaken the child inside of most who read it. It is a story that will have you rooting for not only the children, but the elephant and magician as well. I LOVED the author's last book: The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane, and I must say, DiCamillo has written yet another winner, in my opinion. DON'T MISS IT!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11710932460929435967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=being-yourself">being-yourself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=honesty">honesty</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835207150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18119363640775283847">DiCamillo is so gifted in making the extraordinary elements of who we are and, perhaps, why we are in such a simple way. Her stories, many for younger children, deal with themes of loss and love in ways that open themselves up to the deepest reflections and I love her for it. <br/>When a young boy spends money that is not his in order to have his fortune told, a series of events unfolds in which an elephant is conjured from the air itself. The boy is told that the elephant will lead him to something </span>
  <span id="freeText18119363640775283847" style="display:none">DiCamillo is so gifted in making the extraordinary elements of who we are and, perhaps, why we are in such a simple way. Her stories, many for younger children, deal with themes of loss and love in ways that open themselves up to the deepest reflections and I love her for it. <br />When a young boy spends money that is not his in order to have his fortune told, a series of events unfolds in which an elephant is conjured from the air itself. The boy is told that the elephant will lead him to something important and so the story is set in motion. <br />Again, the accompanying illustrator has been chosen well, with Tanaka’s pictures adding that sense of isolation and warmth which is conjured in the text. DiCamillo as always, never holds her prose back, even from her youngest reader and has created here a marvelously touching and heart-warming story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18119363640775283847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59563497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15896972123862755460">i was so excited for this book. kate dicamillo is probably my favorite author writing right now. after my mother and boyfriends, kate dicamillo is probably the person who can most easily make me cry. if you don't bawl like a baby when winn dixie goes missing you probably have no soul. that said, this book was terribly disappointing. it just tried too hard. dicamillo can write a hauntingly brilliant and touching story about a little girl and her dog. she can write a modern fairy tale like no one </span>
  <span id="freeText15896972123862755460" style="display:none">i was so excited for this book. kate dicamillo is probably my favorite author writing right now. after my mother and boyfriends, kate dicamillo is probably the person who can most easily make me cry. if you don't bawl like a baby when winn dixie goes missing you probably have no soul. that said, this book was terribly disappointing. it just tried too hard. dicamillo can write a hauntingly brilliant and touching story about a little girl and her dog. she can write a modern fairy tale like no one else. and now she's trying insanely hard to write an allegory that just isn't that compelling. i found no urgency in this book, nothing surprising, nothing really touching. if it had been much longer i probably wouldn't have finished it. sigh.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=america">america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=children-s-lit">children-s-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=something-borrowed">something-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=by-women">by-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1231260096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5670182918722685045">A haunting book which would be of interest to adults as well as young people. For some reason, the story made me think of Victor Hugo and his magnum opus, Les Miserables. There is a man whose punishment outweighs the wrong he has done. There are forlorn beggars, wandering children, and orphans in convents. All this makes for plenty of pathos, but there are also lots of humorous touches too. The illustrations add to the enchantment of the narrative.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_326631483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326631483" />
    <a title="shanghao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8606081-shanghao"><img alt="shanghao" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579963873p2/8606081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326631483?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shanghao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shanghao" href="/user/show/8606081-shanghao">shanghao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">parents reading bedtime stories to their children</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8606081-shanghao?shelf=fable">fable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326631483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15238003511842671037">A light, quick read, and might be a suitable bedtime story for more mature children. Reading this as an adult (well I'm not sure I'm one yet but my ID says so in the legal sense), however, doesn't bring much to the table other than light whimsical entertainment value. I like how the illustrations match and complement the story beautifully.<br/><br/>The story tells of Peter, a boy who lives with Vilna-Lutz, an ex-war veteran who took him in after he's orphaned. Peter's days were pretty spartan until one da</span>
  <span id="freeText15238003511842671037" style="display:none">A light, quick read, and might be a suitable bedtime story for more mature children. Reading this as an adult (well I'm not sure I'm one yet but my ID says so in the legal sense), however, doesn't bring much to the table other than light whimsical entertainment value. I like how the illustrations match and complement the story beautifully.<br /><br />The story tells of Peter, a boy who lives with Vilna-Lutz, an ex-war veteran who took him in after he's orphaned. Peter's days were pretty spartan until one day, he made a life-turning choice that led him to embark on a journey to fulfil the most important promise he's made so far, and ultimately finds his true life purpose. Starting with the fortune teller, Peter meets many other characters that in turns guide, inspire, alter his views and help him in his quest.<br /><br />Compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37186.The_Miraculous_Journey_of_Edward_Tulane" title="The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane by Kate DiCamillo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane</a>, this is less magical. The characters are still distinct and charming though, and dependable DiCamillo is adept at gathering empathy even for her less-than-good characters. This is DiCamillo Lite I'd say.<br /><br />The event descriptions are quite structured, with each chapter normally focusing on a character. The plot flows smoothly with some delightful surprises even though the overall storyline is pretty predictable. <br /><br />I imagine myself to be in a quaint little European town full of whimsical elements like Prague, with light symphonies playing in the background. My feeling throughout most of my reading the story were pleasant, but rarely excited or awestruck. It's more of an ambivalent, lullaby-esque kind of story, with just a little bit of hope instilled in you by the end of the book: that all will end well and what's seemingly impossible is possible in small, perhaps even uneventful steps, that can grow more and more miraculous; that there is magic in our everyday lives, and that all it takes is a little belief in the possibility that things can be better, to start it all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15238003511842671037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_62273775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62273775" />
    <a title="Eva Mitnick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/633929-eva-mitnick"><img alt="Eva Mitnick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237933117p2/633929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62273775?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva Mitnick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva Mitnick" href="/user/show/633929-eva-mitnick">Eva Mitnick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/633929-eva-mitnick?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62273775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8355264456163364229">In an allegorical novella reminiscent of an Eastern European fairy tale, young Peter is told by a fortune teller that an elephant will lead him to his long-lostsister. As Peter hadn’t even been certain that his sister was alive, this is excellent news, especially considering his grim life as a sort of apprentice to his guardian, an unbalanced old soldier who has cared for Peter since his parents died.<br/><br/>The only catch is that thre is no elephant in the town of Baltese – until, that is, a magician c</span>
  <span id="freeText8355264456163364229" style="display:none">In an allegorical novella reminiscent of an Eastern European fairy tale, young Peter is told by a fortune teller that an elephant will lead him to his long-lostsister. As Peter hadn’t even been certain that his sister was alive, this is excellent news, especially considering his grim life as a sort of apprentice to his guardian, an unbalanced old soldier who has cared for Peter since his parents died.<br /><br />The only catch is that thre is no elephant in the town of Baltese – until, that is, a magician causes one to fall through the roof of the Bliffendorf Opera House. The sudden and anomalous presence of this elephant has a profound effect on all the people of Baltese, but most especially on Peter, his sister Adele, and a small and eccentric assortment of quietly anguished people.<br /><br />Everything about this slim tale, from the quaint font style (Pabst Oldstyle) to the warm yet somber acrylic illustrations to the almost allegorical appearance of the elephant, brings to mind absurdist Russian/Eastern European tales like Gogol’s The Nose or Kafka’s The Metamorphosis, in which bizarre situations highlight truths about the human condition.<br /><br />I cut my teeth on those kind of stories and so this tale of the fulfillment of heretofore unsuspected or buried hopes and desires felt familiar and comfortable. The writing is smooth, with just enough texture to keep one’s full attention, and the few illustrations I saw in my ARC copy were atmospheric and terrific. However, I can’t see many kids cottoning to the old-fashioned, almost mystical tone of this story, and the characters, including young Peter, remain strangely flat and enigmatic. There was altogether a distant, cool mood to the story that probably won’t appeal to kids who loved The Tale of Despereaux or Because of Wynn Dixie. Still, kids who persevere will be rewarded by an odd yet moving story.<br /><br />Recommended for old souls in grades 4 – 7.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8355264456163364229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VyjFws4Xx1V7s/7X2LT/wz+IUuG6CBcbQrEXM2f4lsiCnGP7AyD3fEIPagNfwp5ZDANljsDeV/a1DXVVfAS0Vg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HKkpg3VXfckU8D0MSz3YWqVa5vs62Vzu3Boi2usitc7JHY+6uGBN4C1MqdjMS7nAltHRlEAPHAMrpkC88N6XUA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13663.Kate_DiCamillo">About Kate DiCamillo</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13663.Kate_DiCamillo"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1402414985p3/13663.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/13663.Kate_DiCamillo">Kate DiCamillo
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
7,170
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17314770062963904048">Kate DiCamillo, the newly named National Ambassador for Young People’s Literature for 2014–2015, says about stories, “When we read together, we connect. Together, we see the world. Together, we see one another.” Born in Philadelphia, the author lives in Minneapolis, where she faithfully writes two pages a day, five days a week.<br/><br/> Kate DiCamillo's own journey is something of a dream come true. After </span>
  <span id="freeText17314770062963904048" style="display:none">Kate DiCamillo, the newly named National Ambassador for Young People’s Literature for 2014–2015, says about stories, “When we read together, we connect. Together, we see the world. Together, we see one another.” Born in Philadelphia, the author lives in Minneapolis, where she faithfully writes two pages a day, five days a week.<br /><br /> Kate DiCamillo's own journey is something of a dream come true. After moving to Minnesota from Florida in her twenties, homesickness and a bitter winter helped inspire Because of Winn-Dixie - her first published novel, which, remarkably, became a runaway bestseller and snapped up a Newbery Honor. "After the Newbery committee called me, I spent the whole day walking into walls," she says. "I was stunned. And very, very happy."<br /><br />Her second novel, The Tiger Rising, went on to become a National Book Award Finalist. Since then, the master storyteller has written for a wide range of ages, including two comical early-chapter-book series - Mercy Watson, which stars a "porcine wonder" with an obsession for buttered toast, and Bink &amp; Gollie, which celebrates the tall and short of a marvelous friendship - as well as a luminous holiday picture book, Great Joy.<br /><br />Her latest novel, Flora &amp; Ulysses: The Illuminated Adventures, won the 2014 Newbery Medal. It was released in fall 2013 to great acclaim, including five starred reviews, and was an instant New York Times bestseller. Flora &amp; Ulysses is a laugh-out-loud story filled with eccentric, endearing characters and featuring an exciting new format - a novel interspersed with comic-style graphic sequences and full-page illustrations, all rendered in black and white by up-and-coming artist K. G. Campbell. It was a 2013 Parents' Choice Gold Award Winner and was chosen by Amazon, Publishers Weekly, Kirkus Reviews, and Common Sense Media as a Best Book of the Year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17314770062963904048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
